In his early years, von Neumann published several papers related to set-theoretical real analysis and number theory.[[184]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-184) In a paper from 1925, he proved that for any dense sequence of points in ![Image 26: {\displaystyle [0,1]}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/738f7d23bb2d9642bab520020873cccbef49768d), there existed a rearrangement of those points that is [uniformly distributed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Equidistributed_sequence "Equidistributed sequence").[[185]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-185)[[186]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-186)[[187]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-187) In 1926 his sole publication was on [Prüfer's](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heinz_Pr%C3%BCfer "Heinz Prüfer") theory of [ideal algebraic numbers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ideal_number "Ideal number") where he found a new way of constructing them, thus extending Prüfer's theory to the [field](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Field_(mathematics) "Field (mathematics)") of all [algebraic numbers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algebraic_number "Algebraic number"), and clarified their relation to [p-adic numbers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/P-adic_number "P-adic number").[[188]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-188)[[189]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUlam19589%E2%80%9310-189)[[190]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-190)[[191]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-191)[[192]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-192) In 1928 he published two additional papers continuing with these themes. The first dealt with [partitioning](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Partition_of_a_set "Partition of a set") an [interval](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interval_(mathematics) "Interval (mathematics)") into [countably](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Countable_set "Countable set") many [congruent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congruence_relation "Congruence relation")[subsets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subset "Subset"). It solved a problem of [Hugo Steinhaus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hugo_Steinhaus "Hugo Steinhaus") asking whether an interval is ![Image 27: {\displaystyle \aleph _{0}}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/721cd7f8c15a2e72ad162bdfa5baea8eef98aab1)-divisible. Von Neumann proved that indeed that all intervals, half-open, open, or closed are ![Image 28: {\displaystyle \aleph _{0}}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/721cd7f8c15a2e72ad162bdfa5baea8eef98aab1)-divisible by translations (i.e. that these intervals can be decomposed into ![Image 29: {\displaystyle \aleph _{0}}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/721cd7f8c15a2e72ad162bdfa5baea8eef98aab1) subsets that are congruent by translation).[[193]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-193)[[194]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWagonTomkowicz201673-194)[[195]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDyson2013156-195)[[196]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-196) His next paper dealt with giving a [constructive proof](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constructive_proof "Constructive proof") without the [axiom of choice](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Axiom_of_choice "Axiom of choice") that ![Image 30: {\displaystyle 2^{\aleph _{0}}}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/779da5db4ed54fa334dd92089cdf1c284e45febb)[algebraically independent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algebraic_independence "Algebraic independence")[reals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_number "Real number") exist. He proved that ![Image 31: {\displaystyle A_{r}=\textstyle \sum _{n=0}^{\infty }2^{2^{[nr]}}\!{\big /}\,2^{2^{n^{2}}}}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1e99e6add4d4be03981b69521acdd64d88301d75) are algebraically independent for ![Image 32: {\displaystyle r>0}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/23cbbcd53bd13620bc53490e3eec42790850b452). Consequently, there exists a perfect algebraically independent set of reals the size of the [continuum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continuum_(set_theory) "Continuum (set theory)").[[197]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-197)[[198]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-198)[[199]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-199)[[200]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWagonTomkowicz2016114-200) Other minor results from his early career include a proof of a [maximum principle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maximum_principle "Maximum principle") for the gradient of a minimizing function in the field of [calculus of variations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calculus_of_variations "Calculus of variations"),[[201]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-201)[[202]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-202)[[203]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-203)[[204]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-204) and a small simplification of [Hermann Minkowski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hermann_Minkowski "Hermann Minkowski")'s theorem for linear forms in [geometric number theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geometry_of_numbers "Geometry of numbers").[[205]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-205)[[206]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-206)[[207]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUlam195810,_23-207) Later in his career together with [Pascual Jordan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascual_Jordan "Pascual Jordan") and [Eugene Wigner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eugene_Wigner "Eugene Wigner") he wrote a foundational paper classifying all [finite-dimensional](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dimension_(vector_space) "Dimension (vector space)")[formally real Jordan algebras](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jordan_algebra#Formally_real_Jordan_algebras "Jordan algebra") and discovering the [Albert algebras](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_algebra "Albert algebra") while attempting to look for a better [mathematical formalism for quantum theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_formulation_of_quantum_mechanics "Mathematical formulation of quantum mechanics").[[208]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-208)[[209]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-209) In 1936 he attempted to further the program of replacing the axioms of his previous Hilbert space program with those of Jordan algebras[[210]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-210) in a paper investigating the infinite-dimensional case; he planned to write at least one further paper on the topic but never did.[[211]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-211) Nevertheless, these axioms formed the basis for further investigations of algebraic quantum mechanics started by [Irving Segal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Irving_Segal "Irving Segal").[[212]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-212)[[213]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-213)

Von Neumann was the first to establish a rigorous mathematical framework for [quantum mechanics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_mechanics "Quantum mechanics"), known as the [Dirac–von Neumann axioms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dirac%E2%80%93von_Neumann_axioms "Dirac–von Neumann axioms"), in his influential 1932 work _[Mathematical Foundations of Quantum Mechanics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical\_Foundations\_of\_Quantum\_Mechanics "Mathematical Foundations of Quantum Mechanics")_.[[214]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-VanHove-214) After having completed the axiomatization of set theory, he began to confront the axiomatization of quantum mechanics. He realized in 1926 that a state of a quantum system could be represented by a point in a (complex) Hilbert space that, in general, could be infinite-dimensional even for a single particle. In this formalism of quantum mechanics, observable quantities such as position or momentum are represented as [linear operators](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linear_operators "Linear operators") acting on the Hilbert space associated with the quantum system.[[215]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacrae1992139%E2%80%93141-215)

The _physics_ of quantum mechanics was thereby reduced to the _mathematics_ of Hilbert spaces and linear operators acting on them. For example, the [uncertainty principle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uncertainty_principle "Uncertainty principle"), according to which the determination of the position of a particle prevents the determination of its momentum and vice versa, is translated into the _non-commutativity_ of the two corresponding operators. This new mathematical formulation included as special cases the formulations of both Heisenberg and Schrödinger.[[215]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacrae1992139%E2%80%93141-215)

Von Neumann's abstract treatment permitted him to confront the foundational issue of determinism versus non-determinism, and in the book he presented a [proof](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_Foundations_of_Quantum_Mechanics#No_hidden_variables_proof "Mathematical Foundations of Quantum Mechanics") that the statistical results of quantum mechanics could not possibly be averages of an underlying set of determined "hidden variables", as in classical statistical mechanics. In 1935, [Grete Hermann](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grete_Hermann "Grete Hermann") published a paper arguing that the proof contained a conceptual error and was therefore invalid.[[216]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-216) Hermann's work was largely ignored until after [John S. Bell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_S._Bell "John S. Bell") made essentially the same argument in 1966.[[217]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-217) In 2010, [Jeffrey Bub](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeffrey_Bub "Jeffrey Bub") argued that Bell had misconstrued von Neumann's proof, and pointed out that the proof, though not valid for all [hidden variable theories](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hidden_variable_theories "Hidden variable theories"), does rule out a well-defined and important subset. Bub also suggests that von Neumann was aware of this limitation and did not claim that his proof completely ruled out hidden variable theories.[[218]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-218) The validity of Bub's argument is, in turn, disputed. [Gleason's theorem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gleason%27s_theorem "Gleason's theorem") of 1957 provided an argument against hidden variables along the lines of von Neumann's, but founded on assumptions seen as better motivated and more physically meaningful.[[219]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-219)[[220]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-220)

Von Neumann's proof inaugurated a line of research that ultimately led, through [Bell's theorem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bell%27s_theorem "Bell's theorem") and the [experiments of Alain Aspect](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aspect%27s_experiment "Aspect's experiment") in 1982, to the demonstration that quantum physics either requires a _notion of reality_ substantially different from that of classical physics, or must include [nonlocality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_nonlocality "Quantum nonlocality") in apparent violation of special relativity.[[221]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-221)

In a chapter of _The Mathematical Foundations of Quantum Mechanics_, von Neumann deeply analyzed the so-called [measurement problem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Measurement_problem "Measurement problem"). He concluded that the entire physical universe could be made subject to the universal [wave function](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wave_function_collapse "Wave function collapse"). Since something "outside the calculation" was needed to collapse the wave function, von Neumann concluded that the collapse was caused by the consciousness of the experimenter. He argued that the mathematics of quantum mechanics allows the collapse of the wave function to be placed at any position in the causal chain from the measurement device to the "subjective consciousness" of the human observer. In other words, while the line between observer and observed could be drawn in different places, the theory only makes sense if an observer exists somewhere.[[222]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-222) Although the idea of [consciousness causing collapse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consciousness_causes_collapse "Consciousness causes collapse") was accepted by Eugene Wigner,[[223]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-Wigner-223) this interpretation never gained acceptance among the majority of physicists.[[224]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-224)

Though theories of quantum mechanics continue to evolve, a basic framework for the mathematical formalism of problems in quantum mechanics underlying most approaches can be traced back to the mathematical formalisms and techniques first used by von Neumann. Discussions about [interpretation of the theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interpretations_of_quantum_mechanics "Interpretations of quantum mechanics"), and extensions to it, are now mostly conducted on the basis of shared assumptions about the mathematical foundations.[[214]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-VanHove-214)

Viewing von Neumann's work on quantum mechanics as a part of the fulfilment of [Hilbert's sixth problem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hilbert%27s_sixth_problem "Hilbert's sixth problem"), mathematical physicist [Arthur Wightman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arthur_Wightman "Arthur Wightman") said in 1974 his axiomization of quantum theory was perhaps the most important axiomization of a physical theory to date. With his 1932 book, quantum mechanics became a mature theory in the sense it had a precise mathematical form, which allowed for clear answers to conceptual problems.[[225]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-225) Nevertheless, von Neumann in his later years felt he had failed in this aspect of his scientific work as despite all the mathematics he developed, he did not find a satisfactory mathematical framework for quantum theory as a whole.[[226]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKacRotaSchwartz2008168-226)[[227]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTER%C3%A9dei200521,_151%E2%80%93152,_194-227)

#### Von Neumann entropy

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=John_von_Neumann&action=edit&section=21 "Edit section: Von Neumann entropy")]

[Von Neumann entropy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Von_Neumann_entropy "Von Neumann entropy") is extensively used in different forms ([conditional entropy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conditional_entropy "Conditional entropy"), [relative entropy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Relative_entropy "Relative entropy"), etc.) in the framework of [quantum information theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_information_theory "Quantum information theory").[[228]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-228) Entanglement measures are based upon some quantity directly related to the von Neumann entropy. Given a [statistical ensemble](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistical_ensemble "Statistical ensemble") of quantum mechanical systems with the [density matrix](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Density_matrix "Density matrix")![Image 33: {\displaystyle \rho }](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1f7d439671d1289b6a816e6af7a304be40608d64), it is given by ![Image 34: {\displaystyle S(\rho )=-\operatorname {Tr} (\rho \ln \rho ).\,}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/bb3fa9fbd2413a92a42f7246b9b45677882de810) Many of the same entropy measures in classical information theory can also be generalized to the quantum case, such as Holevo entropy[[229]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-229) and [conditional quantum entropy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conditional_quantum_entropy "Conditional quantum entropy"). Quantum information theory is largely concerned with the interpretation and uses of von Neumann entropy, a cornerstone in the former's development; the [Shannon entropy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Entropy_(information_theory) "Entropy (information theory)") applies to classical information theory.[[230]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-230)

The formalism of [density operators and matrices](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Density_matrix "Density matrix") was introduced by von Neumann[[231]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-231) in 1927 and independently, but less systematically by [Lev Landau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lev_Landau "Lev Landau")[[232]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-PT-232) and [Felix Bloch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Felix_Bloch "Felix Bloch")[[233]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-Ugo-233) in 1927 and 1946 respectively. The density matrix allows the representation of probabilistic mixtures of quantum states ([mixed states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_state#Mixed_states_of_wave_functions "Quantum state")) in contrast to [wavefunctions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wavefunction "Wavefunction"), which can only represent [pure states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pure_state "Pure state").[[234]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-Hall2013pp419-440-234)

#### Von Neumann measurement scheme

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=John_von_Neumann&action=edit&section=23 "Edit section: Von Neumann measurement scheme")]

The [von Neumann measurement scheme](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Measurement_in_quantum_mechanics#History_of_the_measurement_concept "Measurement in quantum mechanics"), the ancestor of quantum [decoherence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decoherence "Decoherence") theory, represents measurements projectively by taking into account the measuring apparatus which is also treated as a quantum object. The 'projective measurement' scheme introduced by von Neumann led to the development of quantum decoherence theories.[[235]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-235)[[236]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-236)

Von Neumann first proposed a [quantum logic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_logic "Quantum logic") in his 1932 treatise _[Mathematical Foundations of Quantum Mechanics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical\_Foundations\_of\_Quantum\_Mechanics "Mathematical Foundations of Quantum Mechanics")_, where he noted that projections on a [Hilbert space](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hilbert_space "Hilbert space") can be viewed as propositions about physical observables. The field of quantum logic was subsequently inaugurated in a 1936 paper by von Neumann and Garrett Birkhoff, the first to introduce quantum logics,[[237]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-237) wherein von Neumann and Birkhoff first proved that quantum mechanics requires a [propositional calculus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Propositional_calculus "Propositional calculus") substantially different from all classical logics and rigorously isolated a new algebraic structure for quantum logics. The concept of creating a propositional calculus for quantum logic was first outlined in a short section in von Neumann's 1932 work, but in 1936, the need for the new propositional calculus was demonstrated through several proofs. For example, photons cannot pass through two successive filters that are polarized perpendicularly (e.g., horizontally and vertically), and therefore, _[a fortiori](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/A\_fortiori\_argument "A fortiori argument")_, it cannot pass if a third filter polarized diagonally is added to the other two, either before or after them in the succession, but if the third filter is added _between_ the other two, the photons will indeed pass through. This experimental fact is translatable into logic as the _non-commutativity_ of conjunction ![Image 35: {\displaystyle (A\land B)\neq (B\land A)}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/da1b1fe957931560d790288f9123622142b05014). It was also demonstrated that the laws of distribution of classical logic, ![Image 36: {\displaystyle P\lor (Q\land R)={}}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c08ace23b13b76b7e523705a4336b67ebcbf1f41)![Image 37: {\displaystyle (P\lor Q)\land (P\lor R)}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c8f069dfce077ebd42edb9e9f0878f375fbcd929) and ![Image 38: {\displaystyle P\land (Q\lor R)={}}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a9533fd58bd45377e4f3230befcd9f2ae069f07c)![Image 39: {\displaystyle (P\land Q)\lor (P\land R)}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/da23a2336fb3ac4009e66778d233108bba13f128), are not valid for quantum theory.[[238]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-quantum_logic-238)

The reason for this is that a quantum disjunction, unlike the case for classical disjunction, can be true even when both of the disjuncts are false and this is in turn attributable to the fact that it is frequently the case in quantum mechanics that a pair of alternatives are semantically determinate, while each of its members is necessarily indeterminate. Consequently, the [distributive law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Distributive_law "Distributive law") of classical logic must be replaced with a weaker condition.[[238]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-quantum_logic-238) Instead of a distributive lattice, propositions about a quantum system form an [orthomodular lattice](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orthomodular_lattice "Orthomodular lattice") isomorphic to the lattice of subspaces of the Hilbert space associated with that system.[[239]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-Putnam1985-239)

Nevertheless, he was never satisfied with his work on quantum logic. He intended it to be a joint synthesis of formal logic and probability theory and when he attempted to write up a paper for the Henry Joseph Lecture he gave at the [Washington Philosophical Society](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philosophical_Society_of_Washington "Philosophical Society of Washington") in 1945 he found that he could not, especially given that he was busy with war work at the time. During his address at the 1954 [International Congress of Mathematicians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Congress_of_Mathematicians "International Congress of Mathematicians") he gave this issue as one of the unsolved problems that future mathematicians could work on.[[240]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTER%C3%A9dei200530%E2%80%9332-240)[[241]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTER%C3%A9deiSt%C3%B6ltzner200153,_153%E2%80%93154,_168%E2%80%93169-241)

During WWII, Von Neumann made fundamental contributions in the field of [fluid dynamics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fluid_dynamics "Fluid dynamics"), including the classic flow solution to [blast waves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blast_wave "Blast wave") now called [Taylor–von Neumann–Sedov blast wave](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taylor%E2%80%93von_Neumann%E2%80%93Sedov_blast_wave "Taylor–von Neumann–Sedov blast wave") after three scientists who devised it independently,[[242]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-242) and the co-discovery (independently by [Yakov Borisovich Zel'dovich](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yakov_Borisovich_Zel%27dovich "Yakov Borisovich Zel'dovich") and [Werner Döring](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Werner_D%C3%B6ring "Werner Döring")) of the [ZND detonation model](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ZND_detonation_model "ZND detonation model") of explosives.[[243]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-243) During the 1930s, von Neumann became an authority on the mathematics of [shaped charges](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shaped_charges "Shaped charges").[[244]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-244)

Later with [Robert D. Richtmyer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_D._Richtmyer "Robert D. Richtmyer"), von Neumann developed an algorithm defining _artificial [viscosity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Viscosity "Viscosity")_ that improved the understanding of [shock waves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shock_wave "Shock wave"). When computers solved hydrodynamic or aerodynamic problems, they put too many computational grid points at regions of sharp discontinuity (shock waves). The mathematics of artificial viscosity smoothed the shock transition without sacrificing basic physics.[[245]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-245)

Von Neumann soon applied computer modelling to the field, developing software for his ballistics research. During World War II, he approached R. H. Kent, the director of the US Army's [Ballistic Research Laboratory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ballistic_Research_Laboratory "Ballistic Research Laboratory"), with a computer program for calculating a one-dimensional model of 100 molecules to simulate a shock wave. Von Neumann gave a seminar on his program to an audience which included his friend [Theodore von Kármán](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theodore_von_K%C3%A1rm%C3%A1n "Theodore von Kármán"). After von Neumann had finished, von Kármán said "Of course you realize [Lagrange](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph-Louis_Lagrange "Joseph-Louis Lagrange") also used digital models to simulate [continuum mechanics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continuum_mechanics "Continuum mechanics")." Von Neumann had been unaware of Lagrange's _[Mécanique analytique](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/M%C3%A9canique\_analytique "Mécanique analytique")_.[[246]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-mhr1980-246)

[![Image 40](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Neumann_J%C3%A1nos_eml%C3%A9kt%C3%A1bl%C3%A1ja_sz%C3%BCl%C5%91h%C3%A1za_fal%C3%A1n_%28Budapest_V._ker%C3%BClet%2C_B%C3%A1thory_u_26.%29.jpg/250px-Neumann_J%C3%A1nos_eml%C3%A9kt%C3%A1bl%C3%A1ja_sz%C3%BCl%C5%91h%C3%A1za_fal%C3%A1n_%28Budapest_V._ker%C3%BClet%2C_B%C3%A1thory_u_26.%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Neumann_J%C3%A1nos_eml%C3%A9kt%C3%A1bl%C3%A1ja_sz%C3%BCl%C5%91h%C3%A1za_fal%C3%A1n_(Budapest_V._ker%C3%BClet,_B%C3%A1thory_u_26.).jpg)

Von Neumann's memorial plaque on the wall of his birthplace in Budapest, 5th district Báthory u. 26.

While not as prolific in physics as he was in mathematics, he nevertheless made several other notable contributions. His pioneering papers with [Subrahmanyan Chandrasekhar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subrahmanyan_Chandrasekhar "Subrahmanyan Chandrasekhar") on the statistics of a fluctuating [gravitational field](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravitational_field "Gravitational field") generated by [randomly distributed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Probability_distribution "Probability distribution")[stars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Star "Star") were considered a _tour de force_.[[247]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-247) In this paper they developed a theory of two-body relaxation[[248]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-248) and used the [Holtsmark distribution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holtsmark_distribution "Holtsmark distribution") to model[[249]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-249) the [dynamics of stellar systems](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stellar_dynamics "Stellar dynamics").[[250]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-250) He wrote several other unpublished manuscripts on topics in [stellar structure](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stellar_structure "Stellar structure"), some of which were included in Chandrasekhar's other works.[[251]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTETaub1976172%E2%80%93176-251)[[252]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-252) In earlier work led by [Oswald Veblen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oswald_Veblen "Oswald Veblen") von Neumann helped develop basic ideas involving [spinors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spinor "Spinor") that would lead to [Roger Penrose](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roger_Penrose "Roger Penrose")'s [twistor theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Twistor_theory "Twistor theory").[[253]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-253)[[254]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-254) Much of this was done in seminars conducted at the [IAS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Institute_for_Advanced_Study "Institute for Advanced Study") during the 1930s.[[255]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-255) From this work he wrote a paper with [A. H. Taub](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abraham_H._Taub "Abraham H. Taub") and Veblen extending the [Dirac equation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dirac_equation "Dirac equation") to [projective](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Projective_geometry "Projective geometry") relativity, with a key focus on maintaining [invariance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Invariant_(physics) "Invariant (physics)") with regards to coordinate, [spin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spin_(physics) "Spin (physics)"), and [gauge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gauge_theory "Gauge theory") transformations, as a part of early research into potential theories of [quantum gravity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_gravity "Quantum gravity") in the 1930s.[[256]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTERickles202089-256) In the same time period he made several proposals to colleagues for dealing with the problems in the newly created [quantum field theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_field_theory "Quantum field theory") and for [quantizing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantization_(physics) "Quantization (physics)") spacetime; however, both his colleagues and he did not consider the ideas fruitful and did not pursue them.[[257]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTER%C3%A9dei200521%E2%80%9322-257)[[258]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTER%C3%A9deiSt%C3%B6ltzner2001222%E2%80%93224-258)[[259]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTERickles2020202%E2%80%93203-259) Nevertheless, he maintained at least some interest, in 1940 writing a manuscript on the Dirac equation in [de Sitter space](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/De_Sitter_space "De Sitter space").[[260]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTETaub1976177-260)

Von Neumann founded the field of [game theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Game_theory "Game theory") as a mathematical discipline.[[261]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-KuhnTucker-261) He proved his [minimax theorem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minimax#Minimax_theorem "Minimax") in 1928. It establishes that in [zero-sum games](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zero-sum_game "Zero-sum game") with [perfect information](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perfect_information "Perfect information") (i.e., in which players know at each time all moves that have taken place so far), there exists a pair of [strategies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Strategy_(game_theory) "Strategy (game theory)") for both players that allows each to minimize their maximum losses.[[262]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-Game_Theory-262) Such strategies are called _optimal_. Von Neumann showed that their minimaxes are equal (in absolute value) and contrary (in sign). He improved and extended the [minimax theorem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minimax_theorem "Minimax theorem") to include games involving imperfect information and games with more than two players, publishing this result in his 1944 _[Theory of Games and Economic Behavior](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theory\_of\_Games\_and\_Economic\_Behavior "Theory of Games and Economic Behavior")_, written with [Oskar Morgenstern](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oskar_Morgenstern "Oskar Morgenstern"). The public interest in this work was such that _[The New York Times](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_New\_York\_Times "The New York Times")_ ran a front-page story.[[263]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-263) In this book, von Neumann declared that economic theory needed to use [functional analysis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Functional_analysis "Functional analysis"), especially [convex sets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Convex_set "Convex set") and the [topological](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Topology "Topology")[fixed-point theorem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fixed-point_theorem "Fixed-point theorem"), rather than the traditional differential calculus, because the maximum-operator did not preserve differentiable functions.[[261]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-KuhnTucker-261)

Von Neumann's functional-analytic techniques—the use of [duality pairings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dual_space "Dual space") of real [vector spaces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vector_space "Vector space") to represent prices and quantities, the use of [supporting](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supporting_hyperplane "Supporting hyperplane") and [separating hyperplanes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hyperplane_separation_theorem "Hyperplane separation theorem") and convex sets, and fixed-point theory—have been primary tools of mathematical economics ever since.[[264]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-264)

### Mathematical economics

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=John_von_Neumann&action=edit&section=29 "Edit section: Mathematical economics")]

Von Neumann raised the [mathematical level of economics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_economics "Mathematical economics") in several influential publications. For his model of an expanding economy, he proved the existence and uniqueness of an equilibrium using his generalization of the [Brouwer fixed-point theorem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brouwer_fixed-point_theorem "Brouwer fixed-point theorem").[[261]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-KuhnTucker-261) Von Neumann's model of an expanding economy considered the [matrix pencil](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eigendecomposition_of_a_matrix#Generalized_eigenvalue_problem "Eigendecomposition of a matrix")_**A**−λ**B**_ with nonnegative matrices**A** and **B**; von Neumann sought [probability](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Probability_vector "Probability vector")[vectors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Generalized_eigenvector "Generalized eigenvector")_p_ and _q_ and a positive number _λ_ that would solve the [complementarity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Complementarity_theory "Complementarity theory") equation ![Image 41: {\displaystyle p^{T}(A-\lambda B)q=0}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1815f2d5f9fc6972774511f0bdde28b57db89366) along with two inequality systems expressing economic efficiency. In this model, the ([transposed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transpose "Transpose")) probability vector _p_ represents the prices of the goods while the probability vector q represents the "intensity" at which the production process would run. The unique solution _λ_ represents the growth factor which is 1 plus the [rate of growth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_growth "Economic growth") of the economy; the rate of growth equals the [interest rate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interest_rate "Interest rate").[[265]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-265)[[266]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-266)

Von Neumann's results have been viewed as a special case of [linear programming](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linear_programming "Linear programming"), where his model uses only nonnegative matrices. The study of his model of an expanding economy continues to interest mathematical economists.[[267]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-267)[[268]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-268) This paper has been called the greatest paper in mathematical economics by several authors, who recognized its introduction of fixed-point theorems, [linear inequalities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linear_inequality "Linear inequality"), [complementary slackness](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linear_programming#Complementary_slackness "Linear programming"), and [saddlepoint duality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duality_(optimization) "Duality (optimization)").[[269]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoreChakravartyGoodwin1989xi-269) In the proceedings of a conference on von Neumann's growth model, Paul Samuelson said that many mathematicians had developed methods useful to economists, but that von Neumann was unique in having made significant contributions to economic theory itself.[[270]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-270) The lasting importance of the work on general equilibria and the methodology of fixed point theorems is underscored by the awarding of [Nobel prizes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nobel_prize "Nobel prize") in 1972 to [Kenneth Arrow](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kenneth_Arrow "Kenneth Arrow"), in 1983 to [Gérard Debreu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/G%C3%A9rard_Debreu "Gérard Debreu"), and in 1994 to [John Nash](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Forbes_Nash_Jr. "John Forbes Nash Jr.") who used fixed point theorems to establish equilibria for [non-cooperative games](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Non-cooperative_game "Non-cooperative game") and for [bargaining problems](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bargaining_problem "Bargaining problem") in his Ph.D. thesis. Arrow and Debreu also used linear programming, as did Nobel laureates [Tjalling Koopmans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tjalling_Koopmans "Tjalling Koopmans"), [Leonid Kantorovich](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leonid_Kantorovich "Leonid Kantorovich"), [Wassily Leontief](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wassily_Leontief "Wassily Leontief"), [Paul Samuelson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Samuelson "Paul Samuelson"), [Robert Dorfman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Dorfman "Robert Dorfman"), [Robert Solow](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Solow "Robert Solow"), and [Leonid Hurwicz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leonid_Hurwicz "Leonid Hurwicz").[[271]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoreChakravartyGoodwin1989234-271)

Von Neumann's interest in the topic began while he was lecturing at Berlin in 1928 and 1929. He spent his summers in Budapest, as did the economist [Nicholas Kaldor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nicholas_Kaldor "Nicholas Kaldor"); Kaldor recommended that von Neumann read a book by the mathematical economist [Léon Walras](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/L%C3%A9on_Walras "Léon Walras"). Von Neumann noticed that Walras's [General Equilibrium Theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_Equilibrium_Theory "General Equilibrium Theory") and [Walras's law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walras%27s_law "Walras's law"), which led to systems of simultaneous linear equations, could produce the absurd result that profit could be maximized by producing and selling a negative quantity of a product. He replaced the equations by inequalities, introduced dynamic equilibria, among other things, and eventually produced his paper.[[272]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacrae1992250%E2%80%93253-272)

Building on his results on matrix games and on his model of an expanding economy, von Neumann invented the [theory of duality in linear programming](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linear_programming#Duality "Linear programming") when [George Dantzig](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Dantzig "George Dantzig") described his work in a few minutes, and an impatient von Neumann asked him to get to the point. Dantzig then listened dumbfounded while von Neumann provided an hourlong lecture on convex sets, fixed-point theory, and duality, conjecturing the equivalence between matrix games and linear programming.[[273]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-273)

Later, von Neumann suggested a new method of [linear programming](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linear_programming "Linear programming"), using the homogeneous linear system of [Paul Gordan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Gordan "Paul Gordan") (1873), which was later popularized by [Karmarkar's algorithm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karmarkar%27s_algorithm "Karmarkar's algorithm"). Von Neumann's method used a pivoting algorithm between [simplices](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simplex "Simplex"), with the pivoting decision determined by a nonnegative [least squares](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Least_squares "Least squares") subproblem with a convexity constraint ([projecting](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Projection_(linear_algebra)#Orthogonal_projections "Projection (linear algebra)") the zero-vector onto the [convex hull](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Convex_hull "Convex hull") of the active simplex). Von Neumann's algorithm was the first [interior point method](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interior_point_method "Interior point method") of linear programming.[[274]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-George_B_2003-274)

Von Neumann was a founding figure in [computing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computing "Computing"),[[275]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoldstine1980167%E2%80%93178-275) with significant contributions to computing hardware design, to [theoretical computer science](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theoretical_computer_science "Theoretical computer science"), to [scientific computing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scientific_computing "Scientific computing"), and to the [philosophy of computer science](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philosophy_of_computer_science "Philosophy of computer science").

[![Image 42](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Living_Large_--_Argonne%27s_First_Computer_%288056998342%29.jpg/250px-Living_Large_--_Argonne%27s_First_Computer_%288056998342%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Living_Large_--_Argonne%27s_First_Computer_(8056998342).jpg)

The [AVIDAC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AVIDAC "AVIDAC") computer was partially based on the architecture of the [IAS machine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IAS_machine "IAS machine") developed by Von Neumann.

Von Neumann consulted for the Army's [Ballistic Research Laboratory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ballistic_Research_Laboratory "Ballistic Research Laboratory"), most notably on the [ENIAC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ENIAC "ENIAC") project,[[276]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacrae1992279%E2%80%93283-276) as a member of its Scientific Advisory Committee.[[277]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-277) Although the single-memory, stored-program architecture is commonly called [von Neumann architecture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Von_Neumann_architecture "Von Neumann architecture"), the architecture was based on the work of [J. Presper Eckert](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J._Presper_Eckert "J. Presper Eckert") and [John Mauchly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Mauchly "John Mauchly"), inventors of ENIAC and its successor, [EDVAC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/EDVAC "EDVAC"). While consulting for the EDVAC project at the [University of Pennsylvania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania "University of Pennsylvania"), von Neumann wrote an incomplete _[First Draft of a Report on the EDVAC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First\_Draft\_of\_a\_Report\_on\_the\_EDVAC "First Draft of a Report on the EDVAC")_. The paper, whose premature distribution nullified the patent claims of Eckert and Mauchly, described a computer that stored both its data and its program in the same address space, unlike the earliest computers which stored their programs separately on [paper tape](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paper_tape "Paper tape") or [plugboards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plugboard "Plugboard"). This architecture became the basis of most modern computer designs.[[278]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-ENIAC_museum-278)

Next, von Neumann designed the [IAS machine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IAS_machine "IAS machine") at the Institute for Advanced Study in Princeton, New Jersey. He arranged its financing, and the components were designed and built at the [RCA Research Laboratory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sarnoff_Corporation "Sarnoff Corporation") nearby. Von Neumann recommended that the [IBM 701](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IBM_701 "IBM 701"), nicknamed _the defense computer_, include a magnetic drum. It was a faster version of the IAS machine and formed the basis for the commercially successful [IBM 704](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IBM_704 "IBM 704").[[279]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTER%C3%A9dei200573-279)[[280]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDyson2012267%E2%80%93268,_287-280)

[![Image 43](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Flow_chart_of_Planning_and_coding_of_problems_for_an_electronic_computing_instrument%2C_1947.jpg/250px-Flow_chart_of_Planning_and_coding_of_problems_for_an_electronic_computing_instrument%2C_1947.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Flow_chart_of_Planning_and_coding_of_problems_for_an_electronic_computing_instrument,_1947.jpg)

[Flow chart](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flow_chart "Flow chart") from von Neumann's "Planning and coding of problems for an electronic computing instrument", published in 1947

Von Neumann was the inventor, in 1945, of the [merge sort](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Merge_sort "Merge sort") algorithm, in which the first and second halves of an array are each sorted recursively and then merged.[[281]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-281)[[282]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-Papers_J._Neumann_Computing_Computer_Theory._1987,_pp._89-95-282)

As part of Von Neumann's hydrogen bomb work, he and Stanisław Ulam developed simulations for hydrodynamic computations. He also contributed to the development of the [Monte Carlo method](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monte_Carlo_method "Monte Carlo method"), which used [random numbers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithmically_random_sequence "Algorithmically random sequence") to approximate the solutions to complicated problems.[[283]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacrae1992334%E2%80%93335-283)

Von Neumann's algorithm for simulating a [fair coin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fair_coin "Fair coin") with a biased coin is used in the "software whitening" stage of some [hardware random number generators](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hardware_random_number_generator "Hardware random number generator").[[284]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-nbsams-284) Because obtaining "truly" random numbers was impractical, von Neumann developed a form of [pseudorandomness](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pseudorandomness "Pseudorandomness"), using the [middle-square method](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle-square_method "Middle-square method"). He justified this crude method as faster than any other method at his disposal, writing that "Anyone who considers arithmetical methods of producing random digits is, of course, in a state of sin."[[284]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-nbsams-284) He also noted that when this method went awry it did so obviously, unlike other methods which could be subtly incorrect.[[284]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-nbsams-284)

[Stochastic computing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stochastic_computing "Stochastic computing") was introduced by von Neumann in 1953,[[285]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-285) but could not be implemented until advances in computing of the 1960s.[[286]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-286)[[287]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-287) Around 1950 he was also among the first to talk about the [time complexity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Time_complexity "Time complexity") of [computations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computation "Computation"), which eventually evolved into the field of [computational complexity theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_complexity_theory "Computational complexity theory").[[288]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-288)

### Cellular automata, DNA and the universal constructor

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=John_von_Neumann&action=edit&section=34 "Edit section: Cellular automata, DNA and the universal constructor")]

[![Image 44](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Nobili_Pesavento_2reps.png/500px-Nobili_Pesavento_2reps.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Nobili_Pesavento_2reps.png)

The first implementation of von Neumann's self-reproducing universal constructor.[[289]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-Pesavento1995-289) Three generations of machine are shown: the second has nearly finished constructing the third. The lines running to the right are the tapes of genetic instructions, which are copied along with the body of the machines.

[![Image 45](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/50/VonNeumann_CA_demo.gif)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:VonNeumann_CA_demo.gif)

A simple configuration in von Neumann's cellular automaton. A binary signal is passed repeatedly around the blue wire loop, using excited and quiescent _ordinary transmission states_. A confluent cell duplicates the signal onto a length of red wire consisting of _special transmission states_. The signal passes down this wire and constructs a new cell at the end. This particular signal (1011) codes for an east-directed special transmission state, thus extending the red wire by one cell each time. During construction, the new cell passes through several sensitised states, directed by the binary sequence.

Von Neumann's mathematical analysis of the structure of [self-replication](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-replication "Self-replication") preceded the discovery of the structure of DNA.[[290]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-290) Ulam and von Neumann are also generally credited with creating the field of [cellular automata](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cellular_automata "Cellular automata"), beginning in the 1940s, as a simplified mathematical model of biological systems.[[291]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-John_von_Neumann_Cellular_Automata-291)

In lectures in 1948 and 1949, von Neumann proposed a [kinematic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kinematic "Kinematic") self-reproducing automaton.[[292]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-292)[[293]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-293) By 1952, he was treating the problem more abstractly. He designed an elaborate 2D [cellular automaton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cellular_automaton "Cellular automaton") that would automatically make a copy of its initial configuration of cells.[[294]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-294) The [Von Neumann universal constructor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Von_Neumann_universal_constructor "Von Neumann universal constructor") based on the [von Neumann cellular automaton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Von_Neumann_cellular_automaton "Von Neumann cellular automaton") was fleshed out in his posthumous _Theory of Self Reproducing Automata_.[[295]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-TSRA-295) The [von Neumann neighborhood](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Von_Neumann_neighborhood "Von Neumann neighborhood"), in which each cell in a two-dimensional grid has the four orthogonally adjacent grid cells as neighbors, continues to be used for other cellular automata.[[296]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-296)

### Scientific computing and numerical analysis

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=John_von_Neumann&action=edit&section=35 "Edit section: Scientific computing and numerical analysis")]

Considered to be possibly "the most influential researcher in [scientific computing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_science "Computational science") of all time",[[297]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGustafsson201891-297) von Neumann made several contributions to the field, both technically and administratively. He developed the [Von Neumann stability analysis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Von_Neumann_stability_analysis "Von Neumann stability analysis") procedure,[[298]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGustafsson2018101%E2%80%93102-298) still commonly used to avoid errors from building up in [numerical methods for linear partial differential equations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Numerical_methods_for_partial_differential_equations "Numerical methods for partial differential equations").[[299]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGustafsson2018235-299) His paper with [Herman Goldstine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herman_Goldstine "Herman Goldstine") in 1947 was the first to describe [backward error analysis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Error_analysis_(mathematics)#Backward_error_analysis "Error analysis (mathematics)"), although implicitly.[[300]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrezinskiWuytack200127-300) He was also one of the first to write about the [Jacobi method](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jacobi_method "Jacobi method").[[301]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrezinskiWuytack2001216-301) At Los Alamos, he wrote several classified reports on solving problems of [gas dynamics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compressible_flow "Compressible flow") numerically. However, he was frustrated by the lack of progress with [analytic methods](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_analysis "Mathematical analysis") for these [nonlinear](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nonlinear_partial_differential_equation "Nonlinear partial differential equation") problems. As a result, he turned towards computational methods.[[302]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGustafsson2018112%E2%80%93113-302) Under his influence Los Alamos became the leader in computational science during the 1950s and early 1960s.[[303]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-303)

From this work von Neumann realized that computation was not just a tool to [brute force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proof_by_exhaustion "Proof by exhaustion") the solution to a problem numerically, but could also provide insight for solving problems analytically,[[304]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-304) and that there was an enormous variety of scientific and engineering problems towards which computers would be useful, most significant of which were [nonlinear problems](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nonlinear_system "Nonlinear system").[[305]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-305) In June 1945 at the First Canadian Mathematical Congress he gave his first talk on general ideas of how to solve problems, particularly of fluid dynamics numerically.[[246]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-mhr1980-246) He also described how [wind tunnels](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wind_tunnel "Wind tunnel") were actually [analog computers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Analog_computer "Analog computer"), and how digital computers would replace them and bring a new era of fluid dynamics. [Garrett Birkhoff](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Garrett_Birkhoff "Garrett Birkhoff") described it as "an unforgettable sales pitch". He expanded this talk with Goldstine into the manuscript "On the Principles of Large Scale Computing Machines" and used it to promote the support of scientific computing. His papers also developed the concepts of [inverting matrices](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Invertible_matrix "Invertible matrix"), [random matrices](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Random_matrix "Random matrix") and automated [relaxation methods](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Relaxation_(iterative_method) "Relaxation (iterative method)") for solving [elliptic boundary value problems](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elliptic_boundary_value_problem "Elliptic boundary value problem").[[306]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-306)

### Weather systems and global warming

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=John_von_Neumann&action=edit&section=36 "Edit section: Weather systems and global warming")]

As part of his research into possible applications of computers, von Neumann became interested in weather prediction, noting similarities between the problems in the field and those he had worked on during the Manhattan Project.[[307]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEdwards2010115-307) In 1946 von Neumann founded the "Meteorological Project" at the Institute for Advanced Study, securing funding for his project from [the Weather Bureau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Weather_Service "National Weather Service"), the [US Air Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/557th_Weather_Wing "557th Weather Wing") and US Navy weather services.[[308]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-Jonathan_Hill_2013_page_216-308) With [Carl-Gustaf Rossby](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carl-Gustaf_Rossby "Carl-Gustaf Rossby"), considered the leading theoretical meteorologist at the time, he gathered a group of twenty meteorologists to work on various problems in the field. However, given his other postwar work he was not able to devote enough time to proper leadership of the project and little was accomplished.

This changed when a young [Jule Gregory Charney](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jule_Gregory_Charney "Jule Gregory Charney") took up co-leadership of the project from Rossby.[[309]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEdwards2010117%E2%80%93118-309) By 1950 von Neumann and Charney wrote the world's first climate modelling software, and used it to perform the world's first numerical [weather forecasts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weather_forecasting "Weather forecasting") on the ENIAC computer that von Neumann had arranged to be used;[[308]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-Jonathan_Hill_2013_page_216-308) von Neumann and his team published the results as _Numerical Integration of the Barotropic Vorticity Equation_.[[310]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-310) Together they played a leading role in efforts to integrate sea-air exchanges of energy and moisture into the study of climate.[[311]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-311) Though primitive, news of the ENIAC forecasts quickly spread around the world and a number of parallel projects in other locations were initiated.[[312]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEdwards2010126-312)

In 1955 von Neumann, Charney and their collaborators convinced their funders to open the Joint Numerical Weather Prediction Unit (JNWPU) in [Suitland, Maryland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suitland,_Maryland "Suitland, Maryland"), which began routine real-time weather forecasting.[[313]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEdwards2010130-313) Next up, von Neumann proposed a research program for climate modeling:

> The approach is to first try short-range forecasts, then long-range forecasts of those properties of the circulation that can perpetuate themselves over arbitrarily long periods of time, and only finally to attempt forecast for medium-long time periods which are too long to treat by simple hydrodynamic theory and too short to treat by the general principle of equilibrium theory.[[314]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-314)

Positive results of [Norman A. Phillips](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Norman_A._Phillips "Norman A. Phillips") in 1955 prompted immediate reaction and von Neumann organized a conference at Princeton on "Application of Numerical Integration Techniques to the Problem of the General Circulation". Once again he strategically organized the program as a predictive one to ensure continued support from the Weather Bureau and the military, leading to the creation of the General Circulation Research Section (now the [Geophysical Fluid Dynamics Laboratory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geophysical_Fluid_Dynamics_Laboratory "Geophysical Fluid Dynamics Laboratory")) next to the JNWPU.[[315]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEdwards2010152%E2%80%93153-315) He continued work both on technical issues of modelling and in ensuring continuing funding for these projects.[[316]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEdwards2010153,_161,_189%E2%80%93190-316) During the late 19th century, [Svante Arrhenius](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Svante_Arrhenius "Svante Arrhenius") suggested that human activity could cause [global warming](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_warming "Global warming") by adding [carbon dioxide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon_dioxide "Carbon dioxide") to the atmosphere.[[317]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-317) In 1955, von Neumann observed that this may already have begun: "Carbon dioxide released into the atmosphere by industry's burning of [coal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coal "Coal") and oil – more than half of it during the last generation – may have changed the atmosphere's composition sufficiently to account for a general warming of the world by about one degree Fahrenheit."[[318]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacrae199216-318)[[319]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-William_H._Davenport_2016_page_266-319) His research into weather systems and meteorological prediction led him to propose manipulating the environment by spreading colorants on the [polar ice caps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polar_ice_cap "Polar ice cap") to enhance absorption of solar radiation (by reducing the [albedo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albedo "Albedo")).[[320]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacrae1992332-320)[[321]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHeims1980236%E2%80%93247-321)[[320]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacrae1992332-320)[[321]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHeims1980236%E2%80%93247-321) However, he urged caution in any program of atmosphere modification:

> What _could_ be done, of course, is no index to what _should_ be done... In fact, to evaluate the ultimate consequences of either a general cooling or a general heating would be a complex matter. Changes would affect the level of the seas, and hence the habitability of the continental coastal shelves; the evaporation of the seas, and hence general precipitation and glaciation levels; and so on... But there is little doubt that one _could_ carry out the necessary analyses needed to predict the results, intervene on any desired scale, and ultimately achieve rather fantastic results.[[319]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-William_H._Davenport_2016_page_266-319)

He also warned that weather and climate control could have military uses, telling [Congress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Congress "United States Congress") in 1956 that they could pose an even bigger risk than [ICBMs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intercontinental_ballistic_missile "Intercontinental ballistic missile").[[322]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEdwards2010189%E2%80%93191-322)

### Technological singularity hypothesis

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=John_von_Neumann&action=edit&section=37 "Edit section: Technological singularity hypothesis")]

> "The technology that is now developing and that will dominate the next decades is in conflict with traditional, and, in the main, momentarily still valid, geographical and political units and concepts. This is a maturing crisis of technology... The most hopeful answer is that the human species has been subjected to similar tests before and it seems to have a congenital ability to come through, after varying amounts of trouble."

—von Neumann, 1955[[319]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-William_H._Davenport_2016_page_266-319)

The first use of the concept of a [singularity](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/singularity "wiktionary:singularity") in the technological context is attributed to von Neumann,[[323]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-323) who according to Ulam discussed the "ever accelerating progress of technology and changes in the mode of human life, which gives the appearance of approaching some essential singularity in the history of the race beyond which human affairs, as we know them, could not continue."[[324]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-chalmers-324) This concept was later fleshed out in the 1970 book _[Future Shock](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Future\_Shock "Future Shock")_ by [Alvin Toffler](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alvin_Toffler "Alvin Toffler").

[![Image 46](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Vonneumann-john_r.jpg/250px-Vonneumann-john_r.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Vonneumann-john_r.jpg)

Von Neumann's wartime [Los Alamos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Alamos_National_Laboratory "Los Alamos National Laboratory") ID badge photo

Beginning in the late 1930s, von Neumann developed an expertise in explosions—phenomena that are difficult to model mathematically. During this period, he was the leading authority of the mathematics of [shaped charges](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shaped_charge "Shaped charge"), leading him to a large number of military consultancies and consequently his involvement in the [Manhattan Project](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manhattan_Project "Manhattan Project"). The involvement included frequent trips to the project's secret research facilities at the [Los Alamos Laboratory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Alamos_Laboratory "Los Alamos Laboratory") in New Mexico.[[39]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-NYT-39)

Von Neumann made his principal contribution to the [atomic bomb](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_weapon "Nuclear weapon") in the concept and design of the [explosive lenses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_weapon_design "Nuclear weapon design") that were needed to compress the [plutonium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plutonium "Plutonium") core of the [Fat Man](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fat_Man "Fat Man") weapon that was later dropped on [Nagasaki](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nagasaki "Nagasaki").[[325]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJacobsen2015Ch._3-325) While von Neumann did not originate the "[implosion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_weapon_design#Implosion-type_weapon "Nuclear weapon design")" concept, he was one of its most persistent proponents, encouraging its continued development against the instincts of many of his colleagues, who felt such a design to be unworkable. He also eventually came up with the idea of using more powerful shaped charges and less fissionable material to greatly increase the speed of "assembly".[[326]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoddesonHenriksenMeadeWestfall1993130%E2%80%93133,_157%E2%80%93159-326)

When it turned out that there would not be enough [uranium-235](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uranium-235 "Uranium-235") to make more than one bomb, the implosive lens project was greatly expanded and von Neumann's idea was implemented. Implosion was the only method that could be used with the [plutonium-239](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plutonium-239 "Plutonium-239") that was available from the [Hanford Site](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hanford_Site "Hanford Site").[[327]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoddesonHenriksenMeadeWestfall1993239%E2%80%93245-327) He established the design of the [explosive lenses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Explosive_lens "Explosive lens") required, but there remained concerns about "edge effects" and imperfections in the explosives.[[328]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoddesonHenriksenMeadeWestfall1993295-328) His calculations showed that implosion would work if it did not depart by more than 5% from spherical symmetry.[[329]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-329) After a series of failed attempts with models, this was achieved by [George Kistiakowsky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Kistiakowsky "George Kistiakowsky"), and the construction of the Trinity bomb was completed in July 1945.[[330]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoddesonHenriksenMeadeWestfall1993320%E2%80%93327-330)

In a visit to Los Alamos in September 1944, von Neumann showed that the pressure increase from explosion shock wave reflection from solid objects was greater than previously believed if the angle of incidence of the shock wave was between 90° and some limiting angle. As a result, it was determined that the effectiveness of an atomic bomb would be enhanced with detonation some kilometers above the target, rather than at ground level.[[331]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacrae1992209-331)[[332]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoddesonHenriksenMeadeWestfall1993184-332)

[![Image 47](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Implosion_bomb_animated.gif/250px-Implosion_bomb_animated.gif)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Implosion_bomb_animated.gif)

Implosion mechanism

Von Neumann was included in the target selection committee that was responsible for choosing the Japanese cities of [Hiroshima](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hiroshima "Hiroshima") and Nagasaki as the [first targets of the atomic bomb](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atomic_bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki "Atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki"). Von Neumann oversaw computations related to the expected size of the bomb blasts, estimated death tolls, and the distance above the ground at which the bombs should be detonated for optimum shock wave propagation. The cultural capital [Kyoto](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kyoto "Kyoto") was von Neumann's first choice,[[333]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacrae1992242%E2%80%93245-333) a selection seconded by Manhattan Project leader General [Leslie Groves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leslie_Groves "Leslie Groves"). However, this target was dismissed by [Secretary of War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_War "United States Secretary of War")[Henry L. Stimson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henry_L._Stimson "Henry L. Stimson").[[334]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-334)

On July 16, 1945, von Neumann and numerous other Manhattan Project personnel were eyewitnesses to the first test of an atomic bomb detonation, which was code-named [Trinity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trinity_(nuclear_test) "Trinity (nuclear test)"). The event was conducted as a test of the implosion method device, at the [Alamogordo Bombing Range](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alamogordo_Bombing_Range "Alamogordo Bombing Range") in New Mexico. Based on his observation alone, von Neumann estimated the test had resulted in a blast equivalent to 5 [kilotons of TNT](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TNT_equivalent "TNT equivalent") (21[TJ](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Terajoule "Terajoule")) but [Enrico Fermi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enrico_Fermi "Enrico Fermi") produced a more accurate estimate of 10 kilotons by dropping scraps of torn-up paper as the shock wave passed his location and watching how far they scattered. The actual power of the explosion had been between 20 and 22 kilotons.[[335]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoddesonHenriksenMeadeWestfall1993371%E2%80%93372-335) It was in von Neumann's 1944 papers that the expression "kilotons" appeared for the first time.[[336]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacrae1992205-336)

Von Neumann continued unperturbed in his work and became, along with Edward Teller, one of those who sustained the [hydrogen bomb project](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thermonuclear_weapon "Thermonuclear weapon"). He collaborated with [Klaus Fuchs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Klaus_Fuchs "Klaus Fuchs") on further development of the bomb, and in 1946 the two filed a secret patent outlining a scheme for using a fission bomb to compress fusion fuel to initiate [nuclear fusion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_fusion "Nuclear fusion").[[337]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-337) The Fuchs–von Neumann patent used [radiation implosion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radiation_implosion "Radiation implosion"), but not in the same way as is used in what became the final hydrogen bomb design, the [Teller–Ulam design](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Teller%E2%80%93Ulam_design "History of the Teller–Ulam design"). Their work was, however, incorporated into the "George" shot of [Operation Greenhouse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Greenhouse "Operation Greenhouse"), which was instructive in testing out concepts that went into the final design.[[338]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-Bernstein2010-338) The Fuchs–von Neumann work was passed on to the Soviet Union by Fuchs as part of his [nuclear espionage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_espionage "Nuclear espionage"), but it was not used in the Soviets' own, independent development of the Teller–Ulam design. The historian [Jeremy Bernstein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeremy_Bernstein "Jeremy Bernstein") has pointed out that ironically, "John von Neumann and Klaus Fuchs, produced a brilliant invention in 1946 that could have changed the whole course of the development of the hydrogen bomb, but was not fully understood until after the bomb had been successfully made."[[338]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-Bernstein2010-338)

For his wartime services, von Neumann was awarded the [Navy Distinguished Civilian Service Award](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Navy_Distinguished_Civilian_Service_Award "Navy Distinguished Civilian Service Award") in July 1946, and the [Medal for Merit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medal_for_Merit "Medal for Merit") in October 1946.[[339]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacrae1992208-339)

In 1950, von Neumann became a consultant to the [Weapons Systems Evaluation Group](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weapons_Systems_Evaluation_Group "Weapons Systems Evaluation Group"),[[340]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacrae1992350%E2%80%93351-340) whose function was to advise the [Joint Chiefs of Staff](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joint_Chiefs_of_Staff "Joint Chiefs of Staff") and the [United States Secretary of Defense](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_Defense "United States Secretary of Defense") on the development and use of new technologies.[[341]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-341) He also became an adviser to the [Armed Forces Special Weapons Project](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armed_Forces_Special_Weapons_Project "Armed Forces Special Weapons Project"), which was responsible for the military aspects on [nuclear weapons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_weapon "Nuclear weapon").[[340]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacrae1992350%E2%80%93351-340) Over the following two years, he became a consultant across the US government.[[342]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheehan2010182-342) This included the [Central Intelligence Agency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency "Central Intelligence Agency") (CIA), a member of the influential General Advisory Committee of the [Atomic Energy Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Atomic_Energy_Commission "United States Atomic Energy Commission"), a consultant to the newly established [Lawrence Livermore National Laboratory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lawrence_Livermore_National_Laboratory "Lawrence Livermore National Laboratory"), and a member of the [Scientific Advisory Group](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scientific_Advisory_Group "Scientific Advisory Group") of the [United States Air Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Air_Force "United States Air Force")[[340]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacrae1992350%E2%80%93351-340) During this time he became a "superstar" defense scientist at [the Pentagon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Pentagon "The Pentagon"). His authority was considered infallible at the highest levels of the US government and military.[[343]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJacobsen201540-343)

During several meetings of the advisory board of the US Air Force, von Neumann and [Edward Teller](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edward_Teller "Edward Teller") predicted that by 1960 the US would be able to build a hydrogen bomb light enough to fit on top of a rocket. In 1953 [Bernard Schriever](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bernard_Schriever "Bernard Schriever"), who was present at the meeting, paid a personal visit to von Neumann at Princeton to confirm this possibility.[[344]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheehan2010178%E2%80%93179-344) Schriever enlisted [Trevor Gardner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trevor_Gardner
