"Trevor Gardner"), who in turn visited von Neumann several weeks later to fully understand the future possibilities before beginning his campaign for such a weapon in Washington.[[345]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheehan2010199-345) Now either chairing or serving on several boards dealing with strategic missiles and nuclear weaponry, von Neumann was able to inject several crucial arguments regarding potential [Soviet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union "Soviet Union") advancements in both these areas and in strategic defenses against American bombers into government reports to argue for the creation of [ICBMs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intercontinental_ballistic_missile "Intercontinental ballistic missile").[[346]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheehan2010217,_219%E2%80%93220-346) Gardner on several occasions brought von Neumann to meetings with the US Department of Defense to discuss with various senior officials his reports.[[347]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheehan2010221-347) Several design decisions in these reports such as inertial guidance mechanisms would form the basis for all ICBMs thereafter.[[348]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheehan2010259-348) By 1954, von Neumann was also regularly testifying to various [Congressional](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Congress "United States Congress") military subcommittees to ensure continued support for the ICBM program.[[349]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheehan2010273,_276%E2%80%93278-349)

However, this was not enough. To have the ICBM program run at full throttle they needed direct action by the President of the United States.[[350]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheehan2010275,_278-350) They convinced [President Eisenhower](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower "Dwight D. Eisenhower") in a direct meeting in July 1955, which resulted in a presidential directive on September 13, 1955. It stated that "there would be the gravest repercussions on the national security and on the cohesion of the free world" if the Soviet Union developed the ICBM before the US and therefore designated the ICBM project "a research and development program of the highest priority above all others." The Secretary of Defense was ordered to commence the project with "maximum urgency".[[351]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheehan2010287%E2%80%93299-351) Evidence would later show that the Soviets indeed were already testing their own [intermediate-range ballistic missiles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intermediate-range_ballistic_missile "Intermediate-range ballistic missile") at the time.[[352]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheehan2010311-352) Von Neumann would continue to meet the President, including at his home in [Gettysburg, Pennsylvania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gettysburg,_Pennsylvania "Gettysburg, Pennsylvania"), and other high-level government officials as a key advisor on ICBMs until his death.[[353]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAspray1990250-353)

### Atomic Energy Commission

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=John_von_Neumann&action=edit&section=41 "Edit section: Atomic Energy Commission")]

In 1955, von Neumann became a commissioner of the [Atomic Energy Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Atomic_Energy_Commission "United States Atomic Energy Commission") (AEC), which at the time was the highest official position available to scientists in the government.[[354]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHeims1980275-354) (While his appointment formally required that he sever all his other consulting contracts,[[355]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAspray1990244%E2%80%93245-355) an exemption was made for von Neumann to continue working with several critical military committees after the [Air Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Air_Force "United States Air Force") and several key [senators](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Senate "United States Senate") raised concerns.[[353]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAspray1990250-353)) He used this position to further the production of compact hydrogen bombs suitable for [intercontinental ballistic missile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intercontinental_ballistic_missile "Intercontinental ballistic missile") (ICBM) delivery. He involved himself in correcting the severe shortage of [tritium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tritium "Tritium") and [lithium 6](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lithium_6 "Lithium 6") needed for these weapons, and he argued against settling for the intermediate-range missiles that the Army wanted. He was adamant that H-bombs delivered deep into enemy territory by an ICBM would be the most effective weapon possible, and that the relative inaccuracy of the missile would not be a problem with an H-bomb. He said the Russians would probably be building a similar weapon system, which turned out to be the case.[[356]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHeims1980276-356)[[357]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacrae1992367%E2%80%93369-357) While [Lewis Strauss](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lewis_Strauss "Lewis Strauss") was away in the second half of 1955 von Neumann took over as acting chairman of the commission.[[358]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHeims1980282-358)

In his final years before his death from cancer, von Neumann headed the United States government's top-secret ICBM committee, which would sometimes meet in his home. Its purpose was to decide on the feasibility of building an ICBM large enough to carry a thermonuclear weapon. Von Neumann had long argued that while the technical obstacles were sizable, they could be overcome. The [SM-65 Atlas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SM-65_Atlas "SM-65 Atlas") passed its first fully functional test in 1959, two years after his death.[[359]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacrae1992359%E2%80%93365-359) The more advanced [Titan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Titan_(rocket_family) "Titan (rocket family)") rockets were deployed in 1962. Both had been proposed in the ICBM committees von Neumann chaired.[[353]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAspray1990250-353) The feasibility of the ICBMs owed as much to improved, smaller warheads that did not have guidance or heat resistance issues as it did to developments in rocketry, and his understanding of the former made his advice invaluable.[[359]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacrae1992359%E2%80%93365-359)[[353]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAspray1990250-353)

Von Neumann entered government service primarily because he felt that, if freedom and civilization were to survive, it would have to be because the United States would triumph over totalitarianism from [Nazism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazism "Nazism"), [Fascism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fascism "Fascism") and [Soviet Communism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ideology_of_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union "Ideology of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union").[[61]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-whitman-61) During a [Senate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Senate "United States Senate") committee hearing he described his political ideology as "violently [anti-communist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-communism "Anti-communism"), and much more militaristic than the norm".[[360]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlair195796-360)[[361]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPais2006109-361)

[Herman Goldstine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herman_Goldstine "Herman Goldstine") commented on von Neumann's ability to intuit hidden errors and remember old material perfectly.[[362]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoldstine19859%E2%80%9310-362)[[363]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAlbersAlexanderson200881-363) When he had difficulties he would not labor on them; instead, he would go home and sleep on it and come back later with a solution.[[364]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoldstine198516-364) This style, 'taking the path of least resistance', sometimes meant that he could go off on tangents. It also meant that if the difficulty was great from the very beginning, he would simply switch to another problem, not trying to find weak spots from which he could break through.[[365]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUlam197678-365) At times he could be ignorant of the standard mathematical literature, finding it easier to rederive basic information he needed rather than chase references.[[366]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHalmos1973387%E2%80%93388-366)

After [World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II "World War II") began, he became extremely busy with both academic and military commitments. His habit of not writing up talks or publishing results worsened.[[367]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-lax1990-367) He did not find it easy to discuss a topic formally in writing unless it was already mature in his mind; if it was not, he would, in his own words, "develop the worst traits of pedantism and inefficiency".[[368]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTER%C3%A9deiSt%C3%B6ltzner2001168-368)

The mathematician [Jean Dieudonné](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jean_Dieudonn%C3%A9 "Jean Dieudonné") said that von Neumann "may have been the last representative of a once-flourishing and numerous group, the great mathematicians who were equally at home in pure and applied mathematics and who throughout their careers maintained a steady production in both directions".[[161]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDieudonn%C3%A9200890-161) According to Dieudonné, his specific genius was in analysis and "combinatorics", with combinatorics being understood in a very wide sense that described his ability to organize and axiomize complex works that previously seemed to have little connection with mathematics. His style in analysis followed the German school, based on foundations in [linear algebra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linear_algebra "Linear algebra") and [general topology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_topology "General topology"). While von Neumann had an encyclopedic background, his range in pure mathematics was not as wide as [Poincaré](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henri_Poincar%C3%A9 "Henri Poincaré"), [Hilbert](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Hilbert "David Hilbert") or even [Weyl](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hermann_Weyl "Hermann Weyl"): von Neumann never did significant work in [number theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Number_theory "Number theory"), [algebraic topology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algebraic_topology "Algebraic topology"), [algebraic geometry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algebraic_geometry "Algebraic geometry") or [differential geometry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Differential_geometry "Differential geometry"). However, in applied mathematics his work equalled that of [Gauss](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carl_Friedrich_Gauss "Carl Friedrich Gauss"), [Cauchy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Augustin-Louis_Cauchy "Augustin-Louis Cauchy") or [Poincaré](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henri_Poincar%C3%A9 "Henri Poincaré").[[117]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDieudonn%C3%A92008-117)

According to Wigner, "Nobody knows all science, not even von Neumann did. But as for mathematics, he contributed to every part of it except number theory and topology. That is, I think, something unique."[[369]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDyson199877-369) Halmos noted that while von Neumann knew lots of mathematics, the most notable gaps were in algebraic topology and number theory; he recalled an incident where von Neumann failed to recognize the topological definition of a [torus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Torus "Torus").[[370]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHalmos1973389-370) Von Neumann admitted to Herman Goldstine that he had no facility at all in topology and he was never comfortable with it, with Goldstine later bringing this up when comparing him to [Hermann Weyl](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hermann_Weyl "Hermann Weyl"), who he thought was deeper and broader.[[364]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoldstine198516-364)

In his biography of von Neumann, [Salomon Bochner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salomon_Bochner "Salomon Bochner") wrote that much of von Neumann's works in pure mathematics involved finite and infinite dimensional [vector spaces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vector_space "Vector space"), which at the time, covered much of the total area of mathematics. However he pointed out this still did not cover an important part of the mathematical landscape, in particular, anything that involved geometry "in the global sense", topics such as [topology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Topology "Topology"), [differential geometry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Differential_geometry "Differential geometry") and [harmonic integrals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hodge_theory "Hodge theory"), [algebraic geometry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algebraic_geometry "Algebraic geometry") and other such fields. Von Neumann rarely worked in these fields and, as Bochner saw it, had little affinity for them.[[130]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBochner1958441-130)

In one of von Neumann's last articles, he lamented that pure mathematicians could no longer attain deep knowledge of even a fraction of the field.[[371]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUlam19588-371) In the early 1940s, Ulam had concocted for him a doctoral-style examination to find weaknesses in his knowledge; von Neumann was unable to answer satisfactorily a question each in differential geometry, number theory, and algebra. They concluded that doctoral exams might have "little permanent meaning". However, when Weyl turned down an offer to write a history of mathematics of the 20th century, arguing that no one person could do it, Ulam thought von Neumann could have aspired to do so.[[372]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUlam1976291-372)

### Preferred problem-solving techniques

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=John_von_Neumann&action=edit&section=45 "Edit section: Preferred problem-solving techniques")]

Ulam remarked that most mathematicians could master one technique that they then used repeatedly, whereas von Neumann had mastered three:

1.   A facility with the symbolic manipulation of linear operators;
2.   An intuitive feeling for the logical structure of any new mathematical theory;
3.   An intuitive feeling for the combinatorial superstructure of new theories.[[373]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUlam197696-373)

Although he was commonly described as an analyst, he once classified himself an algebraist,[[374]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-374) and his style often displayed a mix of algebraic technique and set-theoretical intuition.[[375]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUlam19589-375) He loved obsessive detail and had no issues with excess repetition or overly explicit notation. An example of this was a paper of his on rings of operators, where he extended the normal functional notation, ![Image 48: {\displaystyle \phi (x)}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/546b660b2f3cfb5f34be7b3ed8371d54f5c74227) to ![Image 49: {\displaystyle \phi ((x))}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f99815edc7cdbc24ddea0304fa24ee91dd32738a). However, this process ended up being repeated several times, where the final result were equations such as ![Image 50: {\displaystyle (\psi ((((a)))))^{2}=\phi ((((a))))}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2aa46f8230e9f9bfd6f561f0219abd80cf20c719). The 1936 paper became known to students as "von Neumann's onion"[[376]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-segal1990-376) because the equations "needed to be peeled before they could be digested". Overall, although his writings were clear and powerful, they were not clean or elegant.[[377]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHalmos1973388-377) Although powerful technically, his primary concern was more with the clear and viable formation of fundamental issues and questions of science rather than just the solution of mathematical puzzles.[[376]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-segal1990-376)

According to Ulam, von Neumann surprised physicists by doing dimensional estimates and algebraic computations in his head with fluency Ulam likened to [blindfold chess](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blindfold_chess "Blindfold chess"). His impression was that von Neumann analyzed physical situations by abstract logical deduction rather than concrete visualization.[[378]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUlam195838-378)

Goldstine compared his lectures to being on glass, smooth and lucid. By comparison, Goldstine thought his scientific articles were written in a much harsher manner, and with much less insight.[[65]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoldstine19857-65)[Halmos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Halmos "Paul Halmos") described his lectures as "dazzling", with his speech clear, rapid, precise and all encompassing. Like Goldstine, he also described how everything seemed "so easy and natural" in lectures but puzzling on later reflection.[[366]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHalmos1973387%E2%80%93388-366) He was a quick speaker: [Banesh Hoffmann](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Banesh_Hoffmann "Banesh Hoffmann") found it very difficult to take notes, even in [shorthand](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shorthand "Shorthand"),[[379]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-379) and [Albert Tucker](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_W._Tucker "Albert W. Tucker") said that people often had to ask von Neumann questions to slow him down so they could think through the ideas he was presenting. Von Neumann knew about this and was grateful for his audience telling him when he was going too quickly.[[380]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTETucker19844-380) Although he did spend time preparing for lectures, he rarely used notes, instead jotting down points of what he would discuss and for how long.[[366]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHalmos1973387%E2%80%93388-366)

Von Neumann was also noted for his [eidetic memory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eidetic_memory "Eidetic memory"), particularly of the symbolic kind. [Herman Goldstine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herman_Goldstine "Herman Goldstine") writes:

> One of his remarkable abilities was his power of absolute recall. As far as I could tell, von Neumann was able on once reading a book or article to quote it back verbatim; moreover, he could do it years later without hesitation. He could also translate it at no diminution in speed from its original language into English. On one occasion I tested his ability by asking him to tell me how _[A Tale of Two Cities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/A\_Tale\_of\_Two\_Cities "A Tale of Two Cities")_ started. Whereupon, without any pause, he immediately began to recite the first chapter and continued until asked to stop after about ten or fifteen minutes.[[381]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoldstine1980167-381)

Von Neumann was reportedly able to memorize the pages of telephone directories. He entertained friends by asking them to randomly call out page numbers; he then recited the names, addresses and numbers therein.[[29]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlair195790-29)[[382]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-382)[Stanisław Ulam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanis%C5%82aw_Ulam "Stanisław Ulam") believed that von Neumann's memory was auditory rather than visual.[[383]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUlam1976147%E2%80%93148-383)

### Mathematical quickness

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=John_von_Neumann&action=edit&section=48 "Edit section: Mathematical quickness")]

Von Neumann's mathematical fluency, calculation speed, and general problem-solving ability were widely noted by his peers. [Paul Halmos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Halmos "Paul Halmos") called his speed "awe-inspiring."[[384]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHalmos1973386-384)[Lothar Wolfgang Nordheim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lothar_Wolfgang_Nordheim "Lothar Wolfgang Nordheim") described him as the "fastest mind I ever met".[[385]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoldstine1980171-385)[Enrico Fermi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enrico_Fermi "Enrico Fermi") told physicist [Herbert L. Anderson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herbert_L._Anderson "Herbert L. Anderson"): "You know, Herb, Johnny can do calculations in his head ten times as fast as I can! And I can do them ten times as fast as you can, Herb, so you can see how impressive Johnny is!"[[386]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-386)[Edward Teller](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edward_Teller "Edward Teller") admitted that he "never could keep up with him",[[387]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-387) and [Israel Halperin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel_Halperin "Israel Halperin") described trying to keep up as like riding a "tricycle chasing a racing car."[[388]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-388)

He had an unusual ability to solve novel problems quickly. [George Pólya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_P%C3%B3lya "George Pólya"), whose lectures at [ETH Zürich](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ETH_Z%C3%BCrich "ETH Zürich") von Neumann attended as a student, said, "Johnny was the only student I was ever afraid of. If in the course of a lecture I stated an unsolved problem, the chances were he'd come to me at the end of the lecture with the complete solution scribbled on a slip of paper."[[389]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-389) When [George Dantzig](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Dantzig "George Dantzig") brought von Neumann an unsolved problem in linear programming "as I would to an ordinary mortal", on which there had been no published literature, he was astonished when von Neumann said "Oh, that!", before offhandedly giving a lecture of over an hour, explaining how to solve the problem using the hitherto unconceived [theory of duality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linear_programming#Duality "Linear programming").[[390]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-390)

A story about von Neumann's encounter with the famous [fly puzzle](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Fly_puzzle&action=edit&redlink=1 "Fly puzzle (page does not exist)")[[391]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-391) has entered [mathematical folklore](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_folklore#Stories,_sayings_and_jokes "Mathematical folklore"). In this puzzle, two bicycles begin 20 miles apart, and each travels toward the other at 10 miles per hour until they collide; meanwhile, a fly travels continuously back and forth between the bicycles at 15 miles per hour until it is squashed in the collision. The questioner asks how far the fly traveled in total; the "trick" for a quick answer is to realize that the fly's individual transits do not matter, only that it has been traveling at 15 miles per hour for one hour. As [Eugene Wigner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eugene_Wigner "Eugene Wigner") tells it,[[392]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-392)[Max Born](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Max_Born "Max Born") posed the riddle to von Neumann. The other scientists to whom he had posed it had laboriously computed the distance, so when von Neumann was immediately ready with the correct answer of 15 miles, Born observed that he must have guessed the trick. "What trick?" von Neumann replied. "All I did was sum the [geometric series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geometric_series "Geometric series")."[[393]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHalmos1973386%E2%80%93387-393)

[Rota](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gian-Carlo_Rota "Gian-Carlo Rota") wrote that von Neumann had "deep-seated and recurring self-doubts".[[394]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTERota199771-394)[John L. Kelley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_L._Kelley "John L. Kelley") reminisced in 1989 that "Johnny von Neumann has said that he will be forgotten while [Kurt Gödel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurt_G%C3%B6del "Kurt Gödel") is remembered with [Pythagoras](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pythagoras "Pythagoras"), but the rest of us viewed Johnny with awe."[[395]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-395) Ulam suggests that some of his self-doubts with regard for his own creativity may have come from the fact he had not discovered several important ideas that others had, even though he was more than capable of doing so, giving the [incompleteness theorems](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/G%C3%B6del%27s_incompleteness_theorems "Gödel's incompleteness theorems") and [Birkhoff's](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_David_Birkhoff "George David Birkhoff")[pointwise ergodic theorem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ergodic_theory#Ergodic_theorems "Ergodic theory") as examples. Von Neumann had a virtuosity in following complicated reasoning and had supreme insights, yet he perhaps felt he did not have the gift for seemingly irrational proofs and theorems or intuitive insights. Ulam describes how during one of his stays at Princeton while von Neumann was working on rings of operators, continuous geometries and quantum logic he felt that von Neumann was not convinced of the importance of his work, and only when finding some ingenious technical trick or new approach did he take some pleasure in it.[[396]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUlam197676%E2%80%9377-396) However, according to Rota, von Neumann still had an "incomparably stronger technique" compared to his friend, despite describing Ulam as the more creative mathematician.[[394]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTERota199771-394)

Nobel Laureate [Hans Bethe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hans_Bethe "Hans Bethe") said "I have sometimes wondered whether a brain like von Neumann's does not indicate a species superior to that of man".[[29]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlair195790-29)[Edward Teller](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edward_Teller "Edward Teller") observed "von Neumann would carry on a conversation with my 3-year-old son, and the two of them would talk as equals, and I sometimes wondered if he used the same principle when he talked to the rest of us."[[397]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-397)[Peter Lax](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_Lax "Peter Lax") wrote "Von Neumann was addicted to thinking, and in particular to thinking about mathematics".[[367]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-lax1990-367)[Eugene Wigner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eugene_Wigner "Eugene Wigner") said, "He understood mathematical problems not only in their initial aspect, but in their full complexity."[[398]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTESzanton199258-398)[Claude Shannon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Claude_Shannon "Claude Shannon") called him "the smartest person I've ever met", a common opinion.[[399]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-399)[Jacob Bronowski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jacob_Bronowski "Jacob Bronowski") wrote "He was the cleverest man I ever knew, without exception. He was a genius."[[400]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-400) Due to his wide reaching influence and contributions to many fields, von Neumann is widely considered a [polymath](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polymath "Polymath").[[401]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-401)[[402]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-402)[[403]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-403)

Wigner noted the extraordinary mind that von Neumann had, and he described von Neumann as having a mind faster than anyone he knew, stating that:[[398]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTESzanton199258-398)

> I have known a great many intelligent people in my life. I knew [Max Planck](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Max_Planck "Max Planck"), [Max von Laue](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Max_von_Laue "Max von Laue"), and [Werner Heisenberg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Werner_Heisenberg "Werner Heisenberg"). [Paul Dirac](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Dirac "Paul Dirac") was my brother-in-law; [Leo Szilard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leo_Szilard "Leo Szilard") and Edward Teller have been among my closest friends; and [Albert Einstein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein "Albert Einstein") was a good friend, too. And I have known many of the brightest younger scientists. But none of them had a mind as quick and acute as Jancsi von Neumann. I have often remarked this in the presence of those men, and no one ever disputed me.

"It seems fair to say that if the influence of a scientist is interpreted broadly enough to include impact on fields beyond science proper, then John von Neumann was probably the most influential mathematician who ever lived," wrote [Miklós Rédei](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mikl%C3%B3s_R%C3%A9dei "Miklós Rédei").[[404]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTER%C3%A9dei20057-404) Peter Lax commented that von Neumann would have won a [Nobel Prize in Economics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Economics "Nobel Prize in Economics") had he lived longer, and that "if there were Nobel Prizes in computer science and mathematics, he would have been honored by these, too."[[405]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTER%C3%A9dei2005xiii-405) Rota writes that "he was the first to have a vision of the boundless possibilities of computing, and he had the resolve to gather the considerable intellectual and engineering resources that led to the construction of the first large computer" and consequently that "No other mathematician in this century has had as deep and lasting an influence on the course of civilization."[[406]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTERota199770-406) He is widely regarded as one of the greatest and most influential mathematicians and scientists of the 20th century.[[407]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-407)

[Neurophysiologist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neurophysiology "Neurophysiology")[Leon Harmon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Harmon "Leon Harmon") described him in a similar manner, calling him the only "true genius" he had ever met: "von Neumann's mind was all-encompassing. He could solve problems in any domain. ... And his mind was always working, always restless."[[408]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-408) While consulting for non-academic projects von Neumann's combination of outstanding scientific ability and practicality gave him a high credibility with military officers, engineers, and industrialists that no other scientist could match. In [nuclear missilery](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_weapon "Nuclear weapon") he was considered "the clearly dominant advisory figure" according to [Herbert York](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herbert_York "Herbert York").[[409]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEYork197185-409) Economist [Nicholas Kaldor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nicholas_Kaldor "Nicholas Kaldor") said he was "unquestionably the nearest thing to a genius I have ever encountered."[[269]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoreChakravartyGoodwin1989xi-269) Likewise, [Paul Samuelson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Samuelson "Paul Samuelson") wrote, "We economists are grateful for von Neumann's genius. It is not for us to calculate whether he was a [Gauss](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carl_Friedrich_Gauss "Carl Friedrich Gauss"), or a [Poincaré](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henri_Poincar%C3%A9 "Henri Poincaré"), or a [Hilbert](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Hilbert "David Hilbert"). He was the incomparable Johnny von Neumann. He darted briefly into our domain and it has never been the same since."[[410]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoreChakravartyGoodwin1989121-410)

[![Image 51](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Von_Neumann_crater_5103_h2_h3.jpg/250px-Von_Neumann_crater_5103_h2_h3.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Von_Neumann_crater_5103_h2_h3.jpg)

The von Neumann crater, on the far side of the Moon

Events and awards named in recognition of von Neumann include the annual [John von Neumann Theory Prize](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann_Theory_Prize "John von Neumann Theory Prize") of the [Institute for Operations Research and the Management Sciences](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Institute_for_Operations_Research_and_the_Management_Sciences "Institute for Operations Research and the Management Sciences"),[[411]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-411)[IEEE John von Neumann Medal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IEEE_John_von_Neumann_Medal "IEEE John von Neumann Medal"),[[412]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-412) and the [John von Neumann Prize](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann_Prize "John von Neumann Prize") of the [Society for Industrial and Applied Mathematics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Society_for_Industrial_and_Applied_Mathematics "Society for Industrial and Applied Mathematics").[[413]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-413) Both the crater [von Neumann](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Von_Neumann_(crater) "Von Neumann (crater)") on the [Moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon "Moon")[[414]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-414) and the asteroid [22824 von Neumann](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/22824_von_Neumann "22824 von Neumann") are named in his honor.[[415]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-415)[[416]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-416)

Von Neumann received awards including the [Medal for Merit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medal_for_Merit "Medal for Merit") in 1947, the [Medal of Freedom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medal_of_Freedom_(1945) "Medal of Freedom (1945)") in 1956,[[417]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-417) and the [Enrico Fermi Award](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enrico_Fermi_Award "Enrico Fermi Award") also in 1956. He was elected a member of multiple honorary societies, including the [American Academy of Arts and Sciences](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Academy_of_Arts_and_Sciences "American Academy of Arts and Sciences") and the [National Academy of Sciences](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Academy_of_Sciences "National Academy of Sciences"), and he held eight honorary doctorates.[[418]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAspray1990246%E2%80%93247-418)[[419]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUlam195841%E2%80%9342-419)[[420]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-420) On May 4, 2005, the [United States Postal Service](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Postal_Service "United States Postal Service") issued the _American Scientists_ commemorative postage stamp series, designed by artist [Victor Stabin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Victor_Stabin "Victor Stabin"). The scientists depicted were von Neumann, [Barbara McClintock](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barbara_McClintock "Barbara McClintock"), [Josiah Willard Gibbs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Josiah_Willard_Gibbs "Josiah Willard Gibbs"), and [Richard Feynman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Feynman "Richard Feynman").[[421]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-421)

[John von Neumann University](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=John_von_Neumann_University&action=edit&redlink=1 "John von Neumann University (page does not exist)")[[hu](https://hu.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neumann_J%C3%A1nos_Egyetem "hu:Neumann János Egyetem")] was established in [Kecskemét](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kecskem%C3%A9t "Kecskemét"), Hungary in 2016, as a successor to Kecskemét College.[[422]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-422)

Von Neumann's first published paper was _On the position of zeroes of certain minimum polynomials_, co-authored with [Michael Fekete](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Fekete "Michael Fekete") and published when von Neumann was 18. At 19, his solo paper _On the introduction of transfinite numbers_ was published.[[423]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDyson2013154-423) He expanded his second solo paper, _An axiomatization of set theory_, to create his PhD thesis.[[424]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDyson2013155-424) His first book, _Mathematical Foundations of Quantum Mechanics_, was published in 1932.[[425]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDyson2013157-425) Following this, von Neumann switched from publishing in German to publishing in English, and his publications became more selective and expanded beyond pure mathematics. His 1942 _Theory of Detonation Waves_ contributed to military research,[[426]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDyson2013158-426) his work on computing began with the unpublished 1946 _On the principles of large scale computing machines_, and his publications on weather prediction began with the 1950 _Numerical integration of the barotropic vorticity equation_.[[427]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDyson2013159-427) Alongside his later papers were informal essays targeted at colleagues and the general public, such as his 1947 _The Mathematician_,[[428]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-428) described as a "farewell to pure mathematics", and his 1955 _Can we survive technology?_, which considered a bleak future including nuclear warfare and deliberate climate change.[[429]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDyson2013159%E2%80%93160-429) His complete works have been compiled into a six-volume set.[[423]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDyson2013154-423)

*   _[The MANIAC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_MANIAC\_(book) "The MANIAC (book)")_, 2023 book about von Neumann
*   [German](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_language "German language"): _[Abenteuer eines Mathematikers](https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abenteuer\_eines\_Mathematikers "de:Abenteuer eines Mathematikers")_ (English title: _Adventures of a Mathematician_), biopic about Stanislaw Ulam also features John von Neumann.

265.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_ref-265)**For this problem to have a unique solution, it suffices that the nonnegative matrices**A** and**B** satisfy an [irreducibility condition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perron%E2%80%93Frobenius_theorem "Perron–Frobenius theorem"), generalizing that of the [Perron–Frobenius theorem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perron%E2%80%93Frobenius_theorem "Perron–Frobenius theorem") of nonnegative matrices, which considers the (simplified) [eigenvalue problem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eigenvalues_and_eigenvectors "Eigenvalues and eigenvectors")**A** − λ **I**_q_ = 0, where the nonnegative matrix _**A**_ must be square and where the [diagonal matrix](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diagonal_matrix "Diagonal matrix")_**I**_ is the [identity matrix](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Identity_matrix "Identity matrix"). Von Neumann's irreducibility condition was called the "whales and [wranglers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wrangler_(University_of_Cambridge) "Wrangler (University of Cambridge)")" hypothesis by [D. G. Champernowne](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/D._G._Champernowne "D. G. Champernowne"), who provided a verbal and economic commentary on the English translation of von Neumann's article. Von Neumann's hypothesis implied that every economic process used a positive amount of every economic good. Weaker "irreducibility" conditions were given by [David Gale](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Gale "David Gale") and by [John Kemeny](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_George_Kemeny "John George Kemeny"), Morgenstern, and [Gerald L. Thompson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gerald_L._Thompson "Gerald L. Thompson") in the 1950s and then by Stephen M. Robinson in the 1970s.
266.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann#cite_ref-266)**[Morgenstern, Oskar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oskar_Morgenstern "Oskar Morgenstern"); [Thompson, Gerald L.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gerald_L._Thompson "Gerald L. Thompson") (1976). [_Mathematical Theory of Expanding and Contracting Economies_](https://archive.org/details/mathematicaltheo0000morg). Lexington Books. Lexington, Massachusetts: D. C. Heath and Company. pp.xviii, 277. [ISBN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISBN_(identifier) "ISBN (identifier)")[978-0-669-00089-4](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-669-00089-4 "Special:BookSources/978-0-669-00089-4").

[University of St Andrews](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_St_Andrews "University of St Andrews").
*   [von Neumann's profile](https://scholar.google.com.au/citations?user=6kEXBa0AAAAJ) at [Google Scholar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Google_Scholar "Google Scholar")
*   [Oral History Project](https://www.math.princeton.edu/about/oral-history) - The Princeton Mathematics Community in the 1930s, contains many interviews that describe contact and anecdotes of von Neumann and others at the Princeton University and Institute for Advanced Study community.
*   Oral history interviews (from the [Charles Babbage Institute](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_Babbage_Institute "Charles Babbage Institute"), [University of Minnesota](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Minnesota "University of Minnesota")) with: [Alice R. Burks and Arthur W. Burks](http://purl.umn.edu/107206); [Eugene P. Wigner](http://purl.umn.edu/107714); and [Nicholas C. Metropolis](http://purl.umn.edu/107493).
*   [zbMATH profile](https://zbmath.org/authors/?q=Neumann%2C+John)
*   [Query for "von neumann"](https://albert.ias.edu/search?von%20neumann=&query=von%20neumann) on the digital repository of the Institute for Advanced Study.
*   [Von Neumann vs. Dirac on Quantum Theory and Mathematical Rigor](https://plato.stanford.edu/entries/qt-nvd/) – from _[Stanford Encyclopedia of Philosophy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanford\_Encyclopedia\_of\_Philosophy "Stanford Encyclopedia of Philosophy")_
*   [Quantum Logic and Probability Theory](https://plato.stanford.edu/entries/qt-quantlog/) - from _Stanford Encyclopedia of Philosophy_
*   [FBI files on John von Neumann released via FOI](https://documents2.theblackvault.com/documents/fbifiles/scientists/johnvonneumann-fbi1.pdf)
*   [Biographical video](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Ml3-kVYLNr8) by David Brailsford (John Dunford Professor Emeritus of computer science at the University of Nottingham)
*   [John von Neumann: Prophet of the 21st Century](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=RuwnywSpl40) 2013 [Arte](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arte "Arte") documentary on John von Neumann and his influence in the modern world (in German and French with English subtitles).
*   [John von Neumann - A Documentary](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=vQp70uqsBV4) 1966 detailed documentary by the [Mathematical Association of America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_Association_of_America "Mathematical Association of America") containing remarks by several of his colleagues including Ulam, Wigner, Halmos, Morgenstern, Bethe, Goldstine, Strauss and Teller.
